# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Firefox DOM Event Dispatch Chain

## Your Task

Trace how a DOM event (e.g., click) is dispatched through the Firefox event system in mozilla/gecko-dev. Find C++ source files implementing: the event creation, the event target identification, the capture/bubble phase traversal, the event listener invocation, and the default action execution.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossrepo domain.

- `sg-evals/firefox--871325b8` (mozilla-firefox/firefox)

74-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've completed a comprehensive analysis of the Firefox DOM event dispatch chain and created the answer file at `/workspace/answer.json`.

## Summary

The analysis traces how a DOM event (e.g., click) flows through Firefox's event system:

1. **Event Creation** - Events are created via `EventDispatcher::CreateEvent()` wrapping WidgetEvents in DOM Event objects

2. **Target Chain Identification** - The system builds an event target chain by recursively calling `GetEventTargetParent()` on each target, starting from the deepest element up to the document root

3. **Capture/Bubble Phase Traversal** - `EventTargetChainItem::HandleEventTargetChain()` implements the three-phase dispatch:
   - **Capture phase**: traverses from root down to target
   - **Target phase**: processes the target itself
   - **Bubble phase**: traverses from target back up to root

4. **Event Listener Invocation** - Multiple classes work together:
   - `EventListenerManager::HandleEvent()` finds listeners
   - `EventListenerManager::HandleEventInternal()` and `HandleEventWithListenerArray()` filter and organize listeners
   - `EventListenerManager::HandleEventSingleListener()` actually invokes each listener

5. **Default Action Execution** - Virtual methods `ActivationBehavior()` (on HTMLInputElement, HTMLButtonElement, etc.) execute element-specific default actions like form submission

6. **Post-Event Processing** - `PostHandleEvent()` allows browser-level handling like focus changes and UI updates

The file includes all critical files, functions, and symbols involved in this comprehensive event dispatch system.

primarily in the `dom/events` directory with central coordination through `EventDispatcher`. A DOM event (e.g., click) follows a well-defined path through event creation, target identification, capture/bubble phase traversal, listener invocation, and default action execution.\\n\\n## Event Creation\\nWhen an event is dispatched, it starts in **EventDispatcher::Dispatch()** (dom/events/EventDispatcher.cpp, line 869). The method accepts a WidgetEvent (low-level platform event) or DOM Event. If needed, a DOM Event is created via **EventDispatcher::CreateEvent()** (dom/events/EventDispatcher.cpp, line 1234), which wraps the WidgetEvent in an appropriate DOM Event class (e.g., MouseEvent, ClickEvent, etc.).\\n\\n## Event Target Chain Identification\\nAfter event creation, an event target chain is built by starting with the initial target and repeatedly calling **GetEventTargetParent()** on each target. This process occurs in **EventDispatcher::Dispatch()** (starting around line 1008) where:\\n\\n1. **EventTargetChainItem::Create()** creates the first chain item for the initial target (line 1009)\\n2. The system calls **GetEventTargetParent()** on the current target through the **EventTargetChainItem** class (line 1063)\\n3. **EventTarget::GetEventTargetParent()** (dom/events/EventTarget.h, line 282) is a virtual method that subclasses implement to identify their parent targets\\n4. Chain building continues until either no parent target exists or **mCanHandle** becomes false\\n5. This creates a complete path from the deepest child element to the document root\\n\\nKey visitor class: **EventChainPreVisitor** (dom/events/EventDispatcher.h, line 113) tracks state during chain construction, including flags for event retargeting and special handling requirements.\\n\\n## Capture/Bubble Phase Traversal\\nThe actual event dispatching occurs in **EventTargetChainItem::HandleEventTargetChain()** (dom/events/EventDispatcher.cpp, line 491), which implements the three-phase event dispatch model:\\n\\n### Capture Phase (line 516-585)\\n- Sets flags: `mInCapturePhase = true`, `mInBubblingPhase = false`\\n- Iterates from the top of the chain down to the target (from parent to child)\\n- Calls **item.HandleEvent()** on each chain item if conditions are met (line 528)\\n- Event propagation can be stopped by checking **PropagationStopped()**\\n\\n### Target Phase (line 587-611)\\n- Sets `mInTargetPhase = true`\\n- Handles the target element itself\\n- Calls **HandleEvent()** twice: once in capture mode, once in bubble mode\\n- After target phase in system group, calls **PostHandleEvent()** (line 609)\\n\\n### Bubble Phase (line 613-649)\\n- Sets `mInBubblingPhase = true`, `mInCapturePhase = false`\\n- Iterates from the target upward through the chain (from child to parent)\\n- Only processes if event has `mBubbles` flag set (line 638)\\n- Calls **PostHandleEvent()** for system group listeners (line 645)\\n\\n## Event Listener Invocation\\nWhen **EventTargetChainItem::HandleEvent()** (dom/events/EventDispatcher.cpp, line 339) is called, it retrieves the event listener manager from the target and delegates to **EventListenerManager::HandleEvent()** (dom/events/EventListenerManager.h, line 435).\\n\\nThe listener invocation chain works as follows:\\n\\n1. **EventListenerManager::HandleEvent()** (line 435) performs fast-path checks to skip processing if:\\n   - No capturing listeners and not in bubbling phase\\n   - No system group listeners but event is in system group\\n   - Untrusted event but no listeners accept untrusted events\\n   - Listener map is empty\\n\\n2. **EventListenerManager::HandleEventInternal()** (dom/events/EventListenerManager.cpp, line 1439) does the actual work:\\n   - Checks for \\\"all events\\\" listeners first (line 1481)\\n   - Gets listeners for the specific event type atom (line 1491)\\n   - Calls **HandleEventWithListenerArray()** for each listener set (line 1493)\\n\\n3. **EventListenerManager::HandleEventWithListenerArray()** (line 1536) iterates through all listeners:\\n   - Creates DOM Event on-demand if not already created (line 1581)\\n   - Filters listeners by phase (capture vs. bubble) and event trustedness\\n   - Handles \\\"once\\\" listeners by removing them before invocation\\n   - Calls **HandleEventSingleListener()** for each matching listener\\n\\n4. **EventListenerManager::HandleEventSingleListener()** (line 1233) actually invokes the listener:\\n   - Sets up the event's currentTarget (line 1237)\\n   - Compiles JavaScript event handlers if needed (line 1261)\\n   - For WebIDL callbacks, calls **listenerHolder.GetWebIDLCallback()->HandleEvent()** (line 1276)\\n   - For XPCOM listeners, calls **listenerHolder.GetXPCOMCallback()->HandleEvent()** (line 1281)\\n   - Handles listener exceptions and returns whether propagation should continue (line 1294)\\n\\n## Default Action Execution\\nAfter the system event group completes, default actions are executed through the activation behavior mechanism:\\n\\n1. **EventDispatcher::Dispatch()** checks if an activation target was set during event chain construction (line 1334)\\n2. If the event wasn't prevented, **chain[activationTargetItemIndex].ActivationBehavior()** is called (line 1340)\\n3. **EventTarget::ActivationBehavior()** (dom/events/EventTarget.h, line 295) is a virtual method that elements implement\\n4. Concrete implementations exist in:\\n   - **HTMLInputElement::ActivationBehavior()** (dom/html/HTMLInputElement.cpp, line 4299) - handles form submission, button clicks\\n   - **HTMLButtonElement::ActivationBehavior()** (dom/html/HTMLButtonElement.cpp, line 315) - handles button clicks and form submission\\n5. If the event was prevented with preventDefault(), **LegacyCanceledActivationBehavior()** is called instead (line 1337)\\n\\n## Post-Event Processing\\nAfter all event phases:\\n\\n1. **EventTargetChainItem::PostHandleEvent()** (dom/events/EventDispatcher.cpp, line 483) is called during system group processing\\n2. Calls **EventTarget::PostHandleEvent()** (dom/events/EventTarget.h, line 326), a virtual method for post-processing\\n3. **EventStateManager::PostHandleEvent()** (dom/events/EventStateManager.cpp, line 3977) performs browser-level default actions:\\n   - Focus management\\n   - Selection changes\\n   - UI state updates\\n   - Context menu handling\\n4. The event's target and related targets are cleared if appropriate (line 1326)\\n5. Event's `mDispatchedAtLeastOnce` flag is set (line 1316)\\n\\n## Key Design Patterns\\n\\n### Visitor Pattern\\nThe system uses visitor objects (`EventChainPreVisitor`, `EventChainPostVisitor`) to pass state through the chain without modifying the chain items directly. This allows each target to communicate information up the chain during construction and back down during dispatch.\\n\\n### Event Retargeting\\nShadow DOM and anonymous content requires event retargeting. The `EventChainPreVisitor` tracks `mEventTargetAtParent` to handle cases where the event target changes as it crosses shadow boundaries.\\n\\n### Event Groups\\nFirefox supports two event groups: default (content) and system (browser internals). The system group runs after the default group, allowing browser code to handle events after JavaScript has processed them.\\n\\n### Listener Type Support\\nThe system supports three listener types:\\n- WebIDL EventListener callbacks (JavaScript addEventListener)\\n- XPCOM nsIDOMEventListener (native Firefox code)\\n- Compiled JavaScript event handlers (onX attributes)\\n\\nThis architecture enables efficient, spec-compliant event handling with browser-level customizations while maintaining a clean separation between event dispatching, listener management, and default action execution.\"\n}\n",

primarily in the `dom/events` directory with central coordination through `EventDispatcher`. A DOM event (e.g., click) follows a well-defined path through event creation, target identification, capture/bubble phase traversal, listener invocation, and default action execution.\\n\\n## Event Creation\\nWhen an event is dispatched, it starts in **EventDispatcher::Dispatch()** (dom/events/EventDispatcher.cpp, line 869). The method accepts a WidgetEvent (low-level platform event) or DOM Event. If needed, a DOM Event is created via **EventDispatcher::CreateEvent()** (dom/events/EventDispatcher.cpp, line 1234), which wraps the WidgetEvent in an appropriate DOM Event class (e.g., MouseEvent, ClickEvent, etc.).\\n\\n## Event Target Chain Identification\\nAfter event creation, an event target chain is built by starting with the initial target and repeatedly calling **GetEventTargetParent()** on each target. This process occurs in **EventDispatcher::Dispatch()** (starting around line 1008) where:\\n\\n1. **EventTargetChainItem::Create()** creates the first chain item for the initial target (line 1009)\\n2. The system calls **GetEventTargetParent()** on the current target through the **EventTargetChainItem** class (line 1063)\\n3. **EventTarget::GetEventTargetParent()** (dom/events/EventTarget.h, line 282) is a virtual method that subclasses implement to identify their parent targets\\n4. Chain building continues until either no parent target exists or **mCanHandle** becomes false\\n5. This creates a complete path from the deepest child element to the document root\\n\\nKey visitor class: **EventChainPreVisitor** (dom/events/EventDispatcher.h, line 113) tracks state during chain construction, including flags for event retargeting and special handling requirements.\\n\\n## Capture/Bubble Phase Traversal\\nThe actual event dispatching occurs in **EventTargetChainItem::HandleEventTargetChain()** (dom/events/EventDispatcher.cpp, line 491), which implements the three-phase event dispatch model:\\n\\n### Capture Phase (line 516-585)\\n- Sets flags: `mInCapturePhase = true`, `mInBubblingPhase = false`\\n- Iterates from the top of the chain down to the target (from parent to child)\\n- Calls **item.HandleEvent()** on each chain item if conditions are met (line 528)\\n- Event propagation can be stopped by checking **PropagationStopped()**\\n\\n### Target Phase (line 587-611)\\n- Sets `mInTargetPhase = true`\\n- Handles the target element itself\\n- Calls **HandleEvent()** twice: once in capture mode, once in bubble mode\\n- After target phase in system group, calls **PostHandleEvent()** (line 609)\\n\\n### Bubble Phase (line 613-649)\\n- Sets `mInBubblingPhase = true`, `mInCapturePhase = false`\\n- Iterates from the target upward through the chain (from child to parent)\\n- Only processes if event has `mBubbles` flag set (line 638)\\n- Calls **PostHandleEvent()** for system group listeners (line 645)\\n\\n## Event Listener Invocation\\nWhen **EventTargetChainItem::HandleEvent()** (dom/events/EventDispatcher.cpp, line 339) is called, it retrieves the event listener manager from the target and delegates to **EventListenerManager::HandleEvent()** (dom/events/EventListenerManager.h, line 435).\\n\\nThe listener invocation chain works as follows:\\n\\n1. **EventListenerManager::HandleEvent()** (line 435) performs fast-path checks to skip processing if:\\n   - No capturing listeners and not in bubbling phase\\n   - No system group listeners but event is in system group\\n   - Untrusted event but no listeners accept untrusted events\\n   - Listener map is empty\\n\\n2. **EventListenerManager::HandleEventInternal()** (dom/events/EventListenerManager.cpp, line 1439) does the actual work:\\n   - Checks for \\\"all events\\\" listeners first (line 1481)\\n   - Gets listeners for the specific event type atom (line 1491)\\n   - Calls **HandleEventWithListenerArray()** for each listener set (line 1493)\\n\\n3. **EventListenerManager::HandleEventWithListenerArray()** (line 1536) iterates through all listeners:\\n   - Creates DOM Event on-demand if not already created (line 1581)\\n   - Filters listeners by phase (capture vs. bubble) and event trustedness\\n   - Handles \\\"once\\\" listeners by removing them before invocation\\n   - Calls **HandleEventSingleListener()** for each matching listener\\n\\n4. **EventListenerManager::HandleEventSingleListener()** (line 1233) actually invokes the listener:\\n   - Sets up the event's currentTarget (line 1237)\\n   - Compiles JavaScript event handlers if needed (line 1261)\\n   - For WebIDL callbacks, calls **listenerHolder.GetWebIDLCallback()->HandleEvent()** (line 1276)\\n   - For XPCOM listeners, calls **listenerHolder.GetXPCOMCallback()->HandleEvent()** (line 1281)\\n   - Handles listener exceptions and returns whether propagation should continue (line 1294)\\n\\n## Default Action Execution\\nAfter the system event group completes, default actions are executed through the activation behavior mechanism:\\n\\n1. **EventDispatcher::Dispatch()** checks if an activation target was set during event chain construction (line 1334)\\n2. If the event wasn't prevented, **chain[activationTargetItemIndex].ActivationBehavior()** is called (line 1340)\\n3. **EventTarget::ActivationBehavior()** (dom/events/EventTarget.h, line 295) is a virtual method that elements implement\\n4. Concrete implementations exist in:\\n   - **HTMLInputElement::ActivationBehavior()** (dom/html/HTMLInputElement.cpp, line 4299) - handles form submission, button clicks\\n   - **HTMLButtonElement::ActivationBehavior()** (dom/html/HTMLButtonElement.cpp, line 315) - handles button clicks and form submission\\n5. If the event was prevented with preventDefault(), **LegacyCanceledActivationBehavior()** is called instead (line 1337)\\n\\n## Post-Event Processing\\nAfter all event phases:\\n\\n1. **EventTargetChainItem::PostHandleEvent()** (dom/events/EventDispatcher.cpp, line 483) is called during system group processing\\n2. Calls **EventTarget::PostHandleEvent()** (dom/events/EventTarget.h, line 326), a virtual method for post-processing\\n3. **EventStateManager::PostHandleEvent()** (dom/events/EventStateManager.cpp, line 3977) performs browser-level default actions:\\n   - Focus management\\n   - Selection changes\\n   - UI state updates\\n   - Context menu handling\\n4. The event's target and related targets are cleared if appropriate (line 1326)\\n5. Event's `mDispatchedAtLeastOnce` flag is set (line 1316)\\n\\n## Key Design Patterns\\n\\n### Visitor Pattern\\nThe system uses visitor objects (`EventChainPreVisitor`, `EventChainPostVisitor`) to pass state through the chain without modifying the chain items directly. This allows each target to communicate information up the chain during construction and back down during dispatch.\\n\\n### Event Retargeting\\nShadow DOM and anonymous content requires event retargeting. The `EventChainPreVisitor` tracks `mEventTargetAtParent` to handle cases where the event target changes as it crosses shadow boundaries.\\n\\n### Event Groups\\nFirefox supports two event groups: default (content) and system (browser internals). The system group runs after the default group, allowing browser code to handle events after JavaScript has processed them.\\n\\n### Listener Type Support\\nThe system supports three listener types:\\n- WebIDL EventListener callbacks (JavaScript addEventListener)\\n- XPCOM nsIDOMEventListener (native Firefox code)\\n- Compiled JavaScript event handlers (onX attributes)\\n\\nThis architecture enables efficient, spec-compliant event handling with browser-level customizations while maintaining a clean separation between event dispatching, listener management, and default action execution.\"\n}\n",
